  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1cc02353-390c-4e90-9826-41a56ce8731d'
      });

  <span id="freeText12589844487965546887" style="display:none"><i>Fallen Too Far</i> was Blaire's story. Now it's time for Rush to share his side.<br /><br />Everyone in Rosemary Beach thinks they know how Rush Finlay and Blaire Wynn fell in love. But Rush is back to tell his side of the story...<br /> <br />Rush has earned every bit of his bad-boy reputation. The three-story beach house, luxury car, and line of girls begging for time between his sheets are the envy of every guy in Rosemary Beach, and Rush handles it all with the laid-back cool of a rock star’s son. All he needs are his best friend, Grant, and his sister, Nan.<br /> <br />Until Blaire Wynn drives into town in her beat-up pickup truck with a pistol under her seat. The Alabama farm girl instantly captures Rush’s attention once he discovers that the angelic beauty is his new stepsister, but he vows to keep his distance. Even if she needs his help. Even if he craves her.<br /> <br />Because Rush knows why Blaire is all alone in the world, forced to ask for help from the father who abandoned her three years ago. And he knows if he gets too close it will destroy Nan, who has a secret connection to Blaire.<br /> <br />He has every reason in the world to stay away from her. Find out why he doesn’t.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {

              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });

  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398416388i/9411134.jpg' alt=' photo 44a92048-07ce-4adc-83a1-9985535d1063_zpsddcbb375.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>My problem with books that I’ve already read from the ‘other’ pov- I feel like I know exactly whats going to happen (because, well, I do) so occasionally I don’t read them. I couldn’t skip this book. I love Rush too much and wanted his pov. <i>Rush Too Far</i> was essentially a re-telling of <i>Fallen Too Far</i> from Rush’s pov. Hearing the story from Rush’s side was much different than Blaire’s. I loved getting inside his head and seeing what he was really thinking... <br/><br/><u>Note to readers- if y</u></span>
  <span id="freeText8423206773377561252" style="display:none"><b>4-4.5 stars!!!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%204/44a92048-07ce-4adc-83a1-9985535d1063_zpsddcbb375.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398416388i/9411134.jpg" alt=" photo 44a92048-07ce-4adc-83a1-9985535d1063_zpsddcbb375.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>My problem with books that I’ve already read from the ‘other’ pov- I feel like I know exactly whats going to happen (because, well, I do) so occasionally I don’t read them. I couldn’t skip this book. I love Rush too much and wanted his pov. <i>Rush Too Far</i> was essentially a re-telling of <i>Fallen Too Far</i> from Rush’s pov. Hearing the story from Rush’s side was much different than Blaire’s. I loved getting inside his head and seeing what he was really thinking... <br><br><u>Note to readers- if you haven’t read Fallen Too Far, there may be some storyline spoilers.</u><br><i>
  <blockquote>Eventually, someone did save me. I didn’t deserve it... I’ve been delivered. By a girl. But she isn’t just a girl. She’s an angel. My angel. A beautiful, strong, fierce, loyal angel who entered my life in a pickup truck, carrying a gun.</blockquote>
</i><br>We all know and love Rush Finlay. Son of a rock star, man whore, he’s that guy. He’s also a devoted brother. And when the person ‘responsible’ for his sisters unhappiness arrives at his home, he’s not sure how to act. He’s attracted to Blaire, but there is no way he can go there. No matter how much he may want her. The more he gets to know her, spends time with her, the more he wants. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%204/80b961e0-3b5b-4754-bf63-ca7280cb3572_zps8dd862ff.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398416388i/9411135.jpg" alt=" photo 80b961e0-3b5b-4754-bf63-ca7280cb3572_zps8dd862ff.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I loved the conflict in Rush’s head throughout the story. Rush was a man who was torn. Torn between his family, and the woman he was starting to fall for. He’s a loyal guy to the few people he truly cares for. Nan (as terrible as she may be) is one of those people. It was nice to see that he really did have a lot of internal conflict about how things were going with Blaire. It made me love him even more. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%204/c60a9923-2ce1-4f19-b9a1-5c7d3f0b53f7_zpse3a249ef.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398416388i/9411136.jpg" alt=" photo c60a9923-2ce1-4f19-b9a1-5c7d3f0b53f7_zpse3a249ef.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Blaire becomes one of those people. One of the ones he is loyal to a fault for. Someone he truly cares for. It puts him in an extremely difficult position. If he’s choosing to be with her, he feels like he’s hurting Nan. But Nan can’t see past herself to see the woman Blaire truly is. That strong, brave, real and exceptional person she’s become. Even with everything she’s been through, she sees the good in others. She still fights to survive no matter what.<br><i>
  <blockquote>She would be fine. I would make sure of it. She’d be motherfucking perfect. I wouldn’t let anyone hurt her. I’d protect her. She didn’t have a father to keep her safe, but she had me. She wasn’t alone. Not anymore. She had me.</blockquote>
</i><br> Rush see’s all that in her and wants to be the one to take care of her. She’s taken care of herself and everyone else for far too long. And even though Rush has never been one to settle down, she might just be the woman to change all that. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%204/56377ffa-340a-42c0-bcdf-1e65b9854de8_zps079053ae.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398416388i/9411137.jpg" alt=" photo 56377ffa-340a-42c0-bcdf-1e65b9854de8_zps079053ae.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><i>Fallen Too Far</i> is one of Abbi’s better books in my opinion, and getting it from Rush’s pov was a real treat. I remember reading <i>Fallen Too Far</i> for the first time. To be honest, I wasn’t the biggest Rush fan the first half of the book or so. I actually liked Grant and Woods much better. It was nice being able to love Rush from cover to cover. I would have loved the first book in dual pov, because I love being inside both characters heads. I think Abbi purposely wrote <i>Fallen Too Far</i> just from Blaire’s pov because we were supposed to fall slowly for Rush. And I’m okay with that!<br><br>For all fans of the ‘Too Far’ series, and everyone out there with a Rush Crush, this his side of the story you won’t want to miss out on! <br><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%204/cc94e426-7e01-4a2f-8047-50101c08e314_zps4d0051b9.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398416388i/9411138.jpg" alt=" photo cc94e426-7e01-4a2f-8047-50101c08e314_zps4d0051b9.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><i>*ARC kindly provided by Atria Books in exchange for an honest review*</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8423206773377561252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13686792296239397368"><b>READ THE OFFICIAL PROLOGUE JUST RELEASED!!!!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385438266i/7149418.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>They say that children have the purest hearts. That children don’t truly hate because they don’t fully understand the emotion. They forgive and forget easily.<br/><br/>They say a lot of bullshit like that because it helps them sleep at night. Such sayings make for good, heart-warming clichés to hang on the walls, to bring out a smile in people passing by.<br/><br/>​I know differently. Children love like no other. They have the capacity to love more fiercely than anyone el</span>
  <span id="freeText13686792296239397368" style="display:none"><b>READ THE OFFICIAL PROLOGUE JUST RELEASED!!!!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385438266i/7149418.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>They say that children have the purest hearts. That children don’t truly hate because they don’t fully understand the emotion. They forgive and forget easily.<br><br>They say a lot of bullshit like that because it helps them sleep at night. Such sayings make for good, heart-warming clichés to hang on the walls, to bring out a smile in people passing by.<br><br>​I know differently. Children love like no other. They have the capacity to love more fiercely than anyone else. That much is true. That much I know. Because I lived it. By the age of ten I knew hate and I knew love. Both all-consuming. Both life-altering. And both completely blinding.<br><br>​Looking back now I wish someone had been there to see how my mother had sown the seed of hate inside of me. Inside of my sister. If someone had been there to save us from the lies and bitterness she allowed to fester within us, then maybe things would have been different. For everyone involved.<br><br>​I never would have acted so foolishly. It wouldn’t have been my fault that a girl was left alone to take care of her ailing mother. It wouldn’t have been my fault that the same girl stood at her mother’s graveside, believing that the last person on earth who loved her was dead. It wouldn’t have been my fault that a man destroyed himself after his life became a broken, hollow shell.<br><br>​But no one saved me.<br><br>​No one saved us.<br><br>​We believed the lies. We held onto our hate, and I alone destroyed an innocent girl’s life.<br><br>​They say you reap what you sow. That’s bullshit, too. Because I should be burning in hell for my sins. I shouldn’t be allowed to wake up every morning with this beautiful woman in my arms, who loves me unconditionally. I shouldn’t get to hold my son and know such a pure joy.<br><br>​But I do.<br><br>​Because, eventually, someone did save me. I didn’t deserve it. Hell, more than anyone it was my sister who needed saving. She hadn’t acted on her hate. She hadn’t manipulated the lives of our family members, not caring about the outcome. But her bitterness still controlled her while I had been delivered. By a girl…<br><br>No, she wasn’t just a girl. She was an angel. My angel. A beautiful, strong, fierce, loyal angel who had entered my life in a pick-up truck, carrying a gun.</span>

<div id="review_1240861910" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1240861910" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1240861910?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=new-adult-mania">new-adult-mania</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=guilty-pleasure-read">guilty-pleasure-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=men-can-be-stupid-sometimes">men-can-be-stupid-sometimes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=3-stars-aint-the-devil">3-stars-aint-the-devil</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1240861910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15251330686331015143">Read this because I needed a Glines fix and it did the trick. It's been so long since I read the first book, I wasn't upset about it being pretty much the same. It was almost kind of like a reread, with a lot more cursing. Was this book worth the $7.99 I paid for it? Not really but that's my choice to make.<br/><br/>Via the Goodreads rating system I gave this a 3 because I liked it, I didn't love it or hate it. 3 stars ain't the devil, people.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer774357253" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7580206224977389777"> <b>4 Rush Stars!</b>	<br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399678335i/9581504._SY540_.jpg' width='300' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is another of those books I will not tell you the story because you probably already it know it by now. And in case you don’t: please go read “Fallen Too Far” before you read this book… and this review, for that matter. <br/>We all know how Blaire and Rush’s story began: with a gun and a very hesitant offer. We saw it through Blaire’s eyes how she forced herself through life with a smile on her face and how she found love in the last place she expected to. Now we’re able to see i</span>
  <span id="freeText7580206224977389777" style="display:none"> <b>4 Rush Stars!</b>	<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399678335i/9581504._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is another of those books I will not tell you the story because you probably already it know it by now. And in case you don’t: please go read “Fallen Too Far” before you read this book… and this review, for that matter. <br>We all know how Blaire and Rush’s story began: with a gun and a very hesitant offer. We saw it through Blaire’s eyes how she forced herself through life with a smile on her face and how she found love in the last place she expected to. Now we’re able to see it through Rush eyes. Why he acted that way and why he kept those secrets. And let me tell you: this story got even better when I’ve read it through his eyes. I didn’t think it was possible. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388683472i/7901653.jpg" width="350" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <b>Rating: </b> 4 Stars. <br> <b>Storyline: </b> What can I tell you that you already ddin’t know? This was a nice companion to one of the best NA series ever. I was expecting a little more, I confess. I was expecting to see more of Rush past life and family to understand better some of his actions. We didn’t have that, there wasn’t any new past story or depth added to this book: it was basically the first book told in Rush POV. It seriously lacked a “further-in-time” epilogue, especially since we all know how their story ended. It was a little disappointing in that aspect, but oh well, I always like a little more Rush. <br> <b>Writing Style: </b> First person, male POV. As all the others books in this series, completely addictive. <br> <b>Character Development: </b> I love, love Rush. He’s one of my favorite male characters of all time, so obviously I liked him. I always like Blaire, even when she’s too sweet and too much of a good girl for her own good. <br> <b>Steam: </b> Some hot scenes. <br> <b>HEA: </b>	<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer672069235" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9558674893290168182">This is Rush's POV from the book, <i>Fallen Too Far</i>, and I really recommend that you read it before this one. You could probably get by without reading it but there's so much more depth to the story if you read the first one, first. <br/><br/><b>Negatives:</b><br/><br/>Well, it <i>is</i> the same story. Sure there are little extra bits here and there such as more interaction between Rush and Grant and Rush and Nat but really nothing else. <br/><br/>I did miss Blaire.   <span id="freeText9558674893290168182" style="display:none">This is Rush's POV from the book, <i>Fallen Too Far</i>, and I really recommend that you read it before this one. You could probably get by without reading it but there's so much more depth to the story if you read the first one, first. <br><br><b>Negatives:</b><br><br>Well, it <i>is</i> the same story. Sure there are little extra bits here and there such as more interaction between Rush and Grant and Rush and Nat but really nothing else. <br><br>I did miss Blaire. Granted we do get some of that emotional intensity from Rush but it's nothing like Blaire's. <br><br>And unfortunately, by already knowing how the story works out, there's no real drama which could also be a good thing. You know how things work out and you're not left with that horrible cliffhanger.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1399767573i/9593854.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Positives:</b><br><br>It's Rush! If you have a Rush Crush, there's <i>nothing</i> like too much. Everything you liked from the first book is here...and more! You get A LOT more of all those sexy, dirty thoughts and talks...and I mean A LOT! ;) <br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380222758i/597122.gif" width="400" height="040" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Favorite quotes</b><br><br>♥ "You need to get your head out of Blaire Wonderland."<br><br>♥ "Don't tell me what to do, Grant." <br><br>He let out a short laugh. "Never, brother. Never."<br><br>♥ "Fuck the friend thing."<br><br>♥ "You're my exception."<br><br>♥ "Mine. Blaire is mine."<br><br>♥ "I believe the word you are looking for is epic," Blaire said.<br><br>♥ "I will always love you. No one will ever compare. You own me, Blaire. My heart and soul are yours."</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11854375853454184258">$8.65 for a book that offered absolutely nothing new? What a joke. I hate when authors put out a new book with the male POV only for it to be the exact same story told all over again. There were no new scenes and honestly all his inner monologue were about things that could be easily grasped from the first book. Really disappointed in this book especially for how high the author priced it. Not worth it at all. </span>

  <span id="freeText13069191073386288959" style="display:none"><br><b>4 Rush Crush Stars</b><br><br>We met Rush in <i>Fallen Too Far</i> and immediately he was the asshole we loved to hate…at least for this girl. I thought he was arrogant and I was pretty pissed that he cock-blocked Woods. Yes I was team Woods. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397277374ra/9257794.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Its okay I gradually fell for Rush throughout the book, which may have been Abbi’s intent, but it wasn’t book love at first read. <br><br>After reading Rush’s POV I actually like him more. Watching his struggle and knowing he was just trying to do the right thing for his family and the girl he was falling for. I completely get Rush now. I also loved how Rush, despite being wealthy, never cared that Blair didn’t look or dress the part of a millionaires girlfriend. <br><br>I picked this up, finally, because I was in a slump and Abbi can usually pull me out of one. Let me tell you it worked. I loved getting to read the sexy scenes from Rush’s POV.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1402043046ra/9886351.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I also love how into Blair he is. <br><br>There are some grammatical errors or use of the wrong words, but I still enjoyed it. It wasn’t so bad that I didn’t know what she was trying to say, just want to note because I know that can kill a book for some. <br><br>Overall, I really enjoyed it and think it was one of her better books. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15034436509809349383">Basically Fallen too Far from Rush's POV. Nothing really much to add to that. If you loved the Fallen too Far series you'll enjoy revisiting the first book through Rush's eyes, especially because I believe Abbi Glines does a very good job of getting the male voice right. There were a few nice nuggets buried in here that you don't get in the original book though I'm not sure how necessary this book really is. I would recommend it for people who really love Rush as a character (I do) and who basic</span>
  <span id="freeText15034436509809349383" style="display:none">Basically Fallen too Far from Rush's POV. Nothing really much to add to that. If you loved the Fallen too Far series you'll enjoy revisiting the first book through Rush's eyes, especially because I believe Abbi Glines does a very good job of getting the male voice right. There were a few nice nuggets buried in here that you don't get in the original book though I'm not sure how necessary this book really is. I would recommend it for people who really love Rush as a character (I do) and who basically don't mind reading the same story twice. It was a super quick read so I'm glad I read it. It's actually the very first time I read one of these "alternate POV installments". Not sure it's something I'll be interested in doing again unless I uber love the story, like in this case. That's all! </span>

In the parts where something was actually happening, it was the same like in the 1st book. The only difference was that it was throu</span>
  <span id="freeText15229428091923820408" style="display:none">I'm still asking myself, why the hell I decided to read this thing. For everyone who thought that this can't be worst than the other books, you are wrong. This was way worst. But after one really exhausting and horrible day, I just needed something really light and non engaging. And honestly it can't get any lighter than this.<br />As far as the plot it was non existing. In the parts where something was actually happening, it was the same like in the 1st book. The only difference was that it was through Rush's point of view. He somehow managed to decrease even the plot that did exist. And that is an accomplishment on it's own. <br />That it's pretty much all I can say about this book. Honestly I'm amazed how little plot can a book have. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15229428091923820408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16026069389407883993" style="display:none">⭐️⭐️⭐️💫 3.5 stars<br /><br />I found Rush to be super annoying in his book. He was overly emotional, almost bipolar. He was also Too Stupid To Live. Actually, all the characters were a little stupid and unrealistic. Luckily, Blaire was a pretty good character, especially compared to the others.<br /><br />Of course Nan really got on my nerves, but I expected that. I wish she got more that was coming for her. <br /><br />I felt like this book didn’t even focus on my favorite parts of the series. It was way more focused on the beginning. It was quite slow paced and a little boring. <br /><br />All in all, I really like books in the hero’s point of view, but this is definitely not my favorite of that kind.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_673934323" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/673934323" />
    <a title="AJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3143126-aj"><img alt="AJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406382884p2/3143126.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/673934323?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AJ" href="/user/show/3143126-aj">AJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer673934323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1111978521434267457"><b><i> “My sweet Blaire. She had shown up and stolen a piece of my heart without opening her mouth. Then she’d consumed me. Taken it all. I had let her have it freely.” </i><br/><br/>And we have a winner!!!!!</b><br/><br/>Sadly, my experience with authors rewriting their books from boy POV has been a bit hit and miss. That’s why I am thrilled to say that Abbi Glines has done a wonderful job with this one! It's Rush Finlay in all of his glory, and it is fantastic!<br/><br/>While we are essentially getting a retelling of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16070903.Fallen_Too_Far__Too_Far___1__Rosemary_Beach___1_' title='Fallen Too Far (Too Far, #1; Rosemary Beach, #1) by Abbi Glines' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fallen Too Far</a>, the</span>
  <span id="freeText1111978521434267457" style="display:none"><b><i> “My sweet Blaire. She had shown up and stolen a piece of my heart without opening her mouth. Then she’d consumed me. Taken it all. I had let her have it freely.” </i><br /><br />And we have a winner!!!!!</b><br /><br />Sadly, my experience with authors rewriting their books from boy POV has been a bit hit and miss. That’s why I am thrilled to say that Abbi Glines has done a wonderful job with this one! It's Rush Finlay in all of his glory, and it is fantastic!<br /><br />While we are essentially getting a retelling of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16070903.Fallen_Too_Far__Too_Far___1__Rosemary_Beach___1_" title="Fallen Too Far (Too Far, #1; Rosemary Beach, #1) by Abbi Glines" rel="nofollow noopener">Fallen Too Far</a>, there is a whole lot of new material in this one, and even though pivotal scenes are repeated, a lot of the story is more behind the scenes sort of stuff – Rush’s interactions with other characters, his take on things with Blaire and, of course, his inner monologue, which I absolutely loved! Rush is an interesting character – spoiled, sexy, rude and crude - so getting the opportunity to be inside of his head in that period when Blaire comes into his life and turns it upside down, and all the chemistry that goes along with it, is sensational!<br /><br /><blockquote><i>The fact that I was suddenly glad that I was shirtless wasn’t good. I shouldn’t care that she was staring at my chest like she wanted a lick. Fuck. Fuck. </i>No!<i> She didn’t want to lick my chest. Where the hell had that idea come from?</i></blockquote><br />Rush is quite the jerk at the beginning of <i>Fallen Too Far</i>, and he and Blaire don’t spend a whole lot of time together, so I particularly loved getting his POV during that part so we could see what was really going on, and just how intensely he was feeling at such an early stage of the story. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>There were no rules where Blaire was concerned. She was on a higher plane, above any rules I had when it came to women. I just wanted her. </i>
</blockquote><br />I love his attempts to keep Blaire at a distance, knowing that his big secret will tear her apart, while at the same time his protective nature over her from the very beginning is gorgeous. I love the way he constantly warned the rest of the boys off. Hilarious!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>I tore my gaze off Blaire to see him staring down at her just as reverently as I was. Fuck that.<br />“Don’t look,” I snapped…<br />Grant let out a laugh. “What the hell does that mean, ‘Don’t look’?”<br />It meant not to fucking look.<br /><br />Woods walked into the kitchen and swung his gaze to me. “You don’t deserve her,” he said coldly.<br />“Neither do you,” I replied.<br /><br />“Why are you ordering food? We’re here to drink and dance with cowboys. Not eat,” Bethy said angrily.<br />She could fuck off.</i>
</blockquote><br />But in the end his feelings are too strong him to resist, and holy hotness!! You thought Rush was hot from Blaire’s POV, just wait until you get into this boy’s head. DAYUM!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>God, she had me. That was it. She had me. I couldn’t let her go. Not now. I was owned.</i>
</blockquote><br />And Grant, OMG, I love Grant! He is also protective of Blaire, but in the ‘pushing her together with Rush’ kind of way that made me love him even more.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Grant met me in the hallway. “She’s hurt. Go fix it,” he said, shooting me an annoyed look as he walked past me and back to the party.</i>
</blockquote><br />I also feel like I came to understand Rush’s tolerance of Nan more, and I felt so awful for him and the guilt he felt for the way Nan was. But Nan was still a bitch of epic proportions – moreso than we realise in the other books, actually! Her constant whining had me feeling mighty stabby, and God, I wish she’d just go away!<br /><br />But this is Rush’s story, and he tells it beautifully! The way he falls for Blaire is beautiful, and his absolute and total devotion to her had me swooning madly. <br /><br /><blockquote><i>“Doesn’t sound like she’s alone anymore”…<br />“She’s not. She never will be. I’ll always be there for her. I’ll keep her safe. I’ll take care of her. She will </i>always<i> have me.<br /></i></blockquote><br />This book covers the exact timeframe of <i>Fallen Too Far</i>, including that epically painful cliffy – and let me tell you, from Rush’s POV… OUCH! It’s a great read for fans of this series, I enjoyed every moment of it.<br /><br />4 Rush-loving stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1111978521434267457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_925018067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/925018067" />
    <a title="Cocktails and Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3769521-cocktails-and-books"><img alt="Cocktails and Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436217947p2/3769521.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/925018067?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cocktails and Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cocktails and Books" href="/user/show/3769521-cocktails-and-books">Cocktails and Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3769521-cocktails-and-books?shelf=2014-reading-challenge">2014-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3769521-cocktails-and-books?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3769521-cocktails-and-books?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer925018067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1739741814992147529">So for those that have read the Rosemary Beach series, specifically Blair and Rush's books, RUSH TOO FAR is Rush's POV for the events in FALLEN TOO FAR. And if you might have been on the fence about how you felt regarding Rush, this version of the events will change your mind.<br/><br/>In Blair's POV of this story, Rush came across as a complete and total ass, but I loved him anyway. You could just tell there was more to him that what he showed. Now I know there was more to him. Here was a guy that was le</span>
  <span id="freeText1739741814992147529" style="display:none">So for those that have read the Rosemary Beach series, specifically Blair and Rush's books, RUSH TOO FAR is Rush's POV for the events in FALLEN TOO FAR. And if you might have been on the fence about how you felt regarding Rush, this version of the events will change your mind.<br /><br />In Blair's POV of this story, Rush came across as a complete and total ass, but I loved him anyway. You could just tell there was more to him that what he showed. Now I know there was more to him. Here was a guy that was left, from a very young age, to feel a paternal sense of responsibility for his little sister while his mother went off and did whatever. He grasped at the little time he had by himself with his dad because it gave him a break and allowed for him to be a boy. When he was with his dad, no one was clinging too him or needed him for anything. So as the story unfolded and we discovered why Rush went in search of Abe, I forgave him (even though I thought I already had) for destroying Blair's family in the name of his sister's happiness. I fell for him a little bit harder because he wasn't the ass he wanted everyone to see. He was a twenty-four year old guy who had way to many people using him and sucking the life out of him. Blair calmed Rush and made him think of his own feelings, rather than worrying about everyone else. And to just get inside his mind....*le sigh*.<br /><br />In my opinion, this was a great addition to Blair and Rush's story. It's always nice to hear the other side and realize, from the very beginning, he was as in to her as she was him. Abbi Glines...bring on some more Rush!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1739741814992147529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_728055529" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/728055529" />
    <a title="Deb Dee (autumn delaney)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14499388-deb-dee-autumn-delaney"><img alt="Deb Dee (autumn delaney)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408814647p2/14499388.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

  <span id="freeText17336499553133150813" style="display:none"><b>From Abbi Gline's Facebook <a href="https://www.facebook.com/abbiglinesauthor/posts/454534781335935" rel="nofollow noopener">post</a>!<br /><br />You can find other teasers <a href="http://mybooksandwhatnots.blogspot.com/p/teasers.html" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE.</a></b><br /><br />TEASER: RUSH TOO FAR<br /><br />I knew exactly the kind of guy Woods was because he was just like me. I wasn’t letting him touch her. He saw her as a conquest and I would kill him before I let him use her. The idea of Blaire doing anything with Woods made my skin crawl. I started moving. I didn’t stop and think about it and I didn’t give a shit if my sister saw me. <br /><br />“There is nothing about you that is unwanted. Even Rush isn’t that damn blind,” Woods told her as he moved closer to her. She was trying to get away from him. <br /><br />“Come here, Blaire.” I said reaching out to take her arm and pull her against me. Woods needed to understand she was with me. I was protecting her. He should go look elsewhere. “I didn’t expect you to come tonight.” I said in her ear. If I had known she was going to walk out of that room looking like something good enough to eat I would have guarded the damn door. <br /><br />“I’m sorry. I thought you said I could come,” she whispered her face turning bright red. I hadn’t meant to embarrass her. She misunderstood me. <br /><br />“I hadn’t expected you to show up dressed like that,” I explained keeping my eyes locked on Woods. <br />I didn’t want to discuss this in front of her but if he pushed me we would.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8829871256809244996">Rush Too Far is basically Fallen Too Far from Rush's POV. I think we can all agree that we could read the phone book from Rush's POV and it would be sexy as hell.<br/><br/>I knew he loved Blaire while reading their books.   <span id="freeText8829871256809244996" style="display:none">Rush Too Far is basically Fallen Too Far from Rush's POV. I think we can all agree that we could read the phone book from Rush's POV and it would be sexy as hell.<br /><br />I knew he loved Blaire while reading their books. I knew that he chose her, but what I didn't know was just how possessive he was of her from the get go. Basically we learn that from the moment Blaire walked into his life, his world became all about her.<br /><br />I will say do not read this book if you have not read Fallen too Far. Not that anyone would, but it has been a while since I read FTF and if I hadn't read it, I could easily see someone saying "I don't like Rush" or I don't feel their connect, because some of the book felt a bit odd if you didn't have first hand knowledge of the way it plays out.. So read the first books before you read this.. <br /><br />BUT I felt that RTF was freaking 10 times hotter than the other books, which is saying something. Rush is a dirty guy in the best possible way!!<br /><br />Also I am really hoping we get Never Too Far from his POV as well.. I will be a happy Rush girl if that happens.. Hint hint Abbi Glines..   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('itqI8Z3WTzxJDbEAC5DpPNfTUXLIDinrwV9WZoA2NCJbIi+GPSf7c7bF4jq/B8ryYEhbDoHoiNMh+P56VzMySg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+zkG4f0E25z90l1odbsKW8VhuRs6g9bZ3d5oa2523jUqwaGWXfVv0wIaDlLBLCmVcvqzZ3Nld+E9ecB3uXPYXQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5307369603953746669">Abbi Glines is a #1 New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal bestselling author of the Rosemary Beach, Sea Breeze, Vincent Boys, Field Party and Existence series. She never cooks unless baking during the Christmas holiday counts. She believes in ghosts and has a habit of asking people if their house is haunted before she goes in it. She drinks afternoon tea because she wants to be Britis</span>
  <span id="freeText5307369603953746669" style="display:none">Abbi Glines is a #1 New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal bestselling author of the Rosemary Beach, Sea Breeze, Vincent Boys, Field Party and Existence series. She never cooks unless baking during the Christmas holiday counts. She believes in ghosts and has a habit of asking people if their house is haunted before she goes in it. She drinks afternoon tea because she wants to be British but alas she was born in Alabama. When asked how many books she has written she has to stop and count on her fingers. When she’s not locked away writing, she is reading, shopping (major shoe and purse addiction), sneaking off to the movies alone, and listening to the drama in her teenagers lives while making mental notes on the good stuff to use later. Don’t judge.<br /><br />You can connect with Abbi online in several different ways. She uses social media to procrastinate.<br /></span>
